2 | P a g e
Introduction
State Dvorak A 4-16-21H-142-96 is located North of Dickinson in Dunn County, North Dakota. Oxy
State A 4-16-21H is a single horizontal Middle Bakken well. It will consist of one 20,247' MD
(measured depth) long lateral drilled to the South (181.12º). The vertical hole was drilled to a kick off
point depth of 10,038' MD. The Curve section of the well landed at a measured depth of 11,038' MD,
10,579.21' TVD (total vertical depth), with 29'of rat hole. Intermediate 7"casing was set at 11,009' MD.
Following pre-lateral meeting, drilling of the lateral section began on 10/29/2014. To isolate the targeted
reservoir, a 6" bit was utilized while drilling the lateral section. Upon landing the curve, directional
drilling and geo-steering techniques were employed to maintain maximum exposure to the target
reservoir.
Off Set Wells
MWD Gamma Data was used to determine marker and formation tops during the vertical hole and
during the curve. During both the vertical and curve-build sections, tops were compared to the State
Dvorak 1-17 hole to ensure successful landing within the targeted zone. The true vertical depth (TVD)
of the landing target was calculated by assuming comparable formation thicknesses to the Dvorak 1-17
hole and was adjusted as necessary until landing. Formation dips were predicted but not always accurate
compared to Dvorak 1-17 and the Sharon Rainey 2-17 laterals.
Engineering
Vertical Operations
The State Dvorak A 4-16-21H-142-96 was spud on November 10th, 2014 by H&P 329. An 8 3/4"Smith
MDSi616 (bit #2) was used in front of a 1.5º fixed Hunting mud motor that drill from surface casing of
2,283' MD to 8,631', for a total of 6,348'. At 8,631' tripped out of the hole due to slow ROP, and
changed out BHA (bottom hole assemble). Tripped back in with an 8 3/4" Smith MDSi616 (bit #3) that
drilled to Kick off point of 10,038', for a total of 1,407'. DHI geologists commenced logging at
8,000'MD.
Curve Build
Curve building started on November 20th, 2014 with an 8 ¾" Smith MDi516 (bit#4) and a 2.38 degree
motor which drilled to10,575' before it started to lose build rates and needed to be switched out. An 8
3/4" PDC Smith F30T drilled to landing TD of 11,038'MD in 53 hours. The MWD tool assemblies were
provided by Baker Hughes which recorded survey and gamma ray data. Gamma correlation was good
with some natural variation from the cross-borehole references. The wellbore successfully penetrated the
Middle Bakken formation at 10,789'MD (10,576' TVD). The Curve was landed at 11,038'MD
(10,579.21' TVD) approximately 3' into target zone. Upon completion of the landing, the drill string
and BHA were tripped out of the hole. 7" Casing was set at 11,009'MD.
3 | P a g e
Lateral
The State Dvorak A 4-16-21H-142-96 lateral began on November 26th, 2014 using brine water. The
target interval chosen for this well was 8-14' below the Upper Bakken Shale within an 18' zone. Drilling
of the lateral portion of the well began at a depth of 11,038'MD, with Bit #6 and drilled to a total depth
of 18,517'MD which at that point the MWD tool failed and needed to be tripped out of the hole. Bit# 7 a
PDC HCC T406 finished off that lateral by drilling to 20,247' for a total of 1,730'. The well bore finish
100% in the Middle Bakken formation and 59.2% within the 6' target area of the payzone which is
discussed more under geo-steering section. (Page 9)
Gas Readings
Methods
One well-site geologist and two logging geologists, contracted by DHI Services, Inc. conducted the
geologic analysis for State Dvorak A 4-16-21H-142-96. DHI installed and monitored a flame ionization
detector (FID) Total Hydrocarbon Analyzer (THA) and chromatograph interfaced with a DHI Services, Inc.
Drillsense Electronic Data Recording System (EDR). The EDR provided depth, drilling rate and pump
stroke data to the Clarity-Lite gas-monitoring software which returned gas data in the form of total gas units
and the hydrocarbon components C1 through C5 (methane, ethane, propane, butane and pentane)
concentrations expressed in parts-per-million. Total Gas and the individual components were calibrated
daily to a known calibration gas. (Figure 1)
Figure 1 ­ DHI Services, Inc. Calibration Chromatography
4 | P a g e
DHI's chromatograph reads 7 gases: C-1 methane, C-2 ethane, C-3 propane, iC-4 isobutane, nC-4 normal
butane, iC-5 isopentane, and nC-5 normal pentane. The chromatograph runs continuously automatically,
injecting gas samples and sending the results to clarity light for computation. The results are all tagged with
a time which is then used to populate the database with chromatograph data that is correctly lagged to the
correct foot base on what the lag depth was at the particular time the sample was taken. The chromatograph
uses a coiled column which separates the gases based on molecular weights and is run thru a flame
ionization detector which causes an electrical charge on each carbon atom that is read by the detector and
sent to the clarity light program. The electrical response is compared to the known calibration values. The
chromatograph has various settings that can be change for hi or low gas values.
DHI's THA (Total Hydrocarbon Analyzer) uses the same type of flame ionization detector but detects the
constant stream of gas sample being brought back to the machine via agitator and poly flow sample line.
Because the THA and GC are using the same gas stream there is a constant comparison of each machines
readings. Generally the amount read by the GC, if combined, is roughly the same methane equivalent as
detected by the THA, although there are other gases read by the THA that are not being computed on the
chromatograph such as acetylene and any gas above C-5. This being said the THA will read slightly more
gas compared the methane equivalent of all the gases reported on the mud log's chromatograph data.
Gas samples were pulled through ¼" poly-flow tubing after agitation in DHI's gas trap installed in the
possum belly. DHI personnel caught lagged samples under the supervision of well-site geologists in 10' to
30' intervals from 8,000' to 20,247' TD. Cuttings were then repeatedly washed with Dawn dish detergent
and water until clean. Dry cuttings were examined under a binocular microscope. Cuttings collected from
within the Middle Bakken Formation were evaluated for hydrocarbon fluorescence using a fluoroscope,
"cut" and residual ring.
If more than one carbonate type is present then they can be determined separately using the values from the
multiple pressure peaks and formulas supplied by the instrument manufacturer. Two sets of dry cuttings
were collected, with one set sent to the North Dakota Geological Survey Core Library and the second set
sent to the project geologist overseeing operations.
5 | P a g e
Lithology
Sample analysis began at 8,000' MD in the Amsden
Formation.
The Amsden Formation typically consists of red-brown to red-
orange Limestone, siltstone and shale. It ranges in thickness from
300 ­ 400 feet thick. Typical sample descriptions from this
formation are as follows: SHALE ­ dark red to reddish brown to
green, soft to very soft and platy to sub platy, slightly calcareous,
trace of siltstone.
Amsden Formation
Tyler Formation ­ SHALE- dark red to reddish brown- dark
gray- green-yellow, soft to very soft, and platy to blocky, slightly
calcareous, inner bedded sand stones
6 | P a g e
Tyler Formation
The Mississippian Kibbey Formation typically consists of red-
brown to red-orange sand, siltstone and shale with a limestone
zone near the middle. The upper portion typically consists of
sands inter-bedded with shale while the middle portion is mainly
white to light tan limestone. In this area, the limestone member is
predominant. Typical sample descriptions from this formation are
as follows: LIMESTONE ­dark red to red brown to red gray,
microcrystalline to very fine crystalline, varying hardness from
friable to moderately firm, earthy to dense texture with SHALE
stringers.
Kibbey Formation
Below the Kibbey is the Mississippian Charles Formation
(Madison Group). This formation consists of inter-bedded thick
to thin beds of limestone anhydrite, and salt. Note: Very
important formation in the Williston Basin. Pay particular
attention to the Base of the last salts for target changes. Typical
sample descriptions from this formation are as follows:
LIMESTONE­ light gray to gray to tan gray, cryptocrystalline to
microcrystalline to crystalline, varying hardness from friable to
hard, earthy to dense texture commonly containing anhydrite and
clear crystalline salt.
First Charles Salts
The Mississippian Mission Canyon Formation (Mississippian
Madison Group) is typically composed of mostly massive brown
to gray limestone, argillaceous, fossiliferous and oolitic;
dolomitic in part.
Mission Canyon Formation
The Mississippian Lodgepole Formation (Mississippian
Madison Group) is typically described thin bedded argillaceous
fossiliferous limestone. Typical sample descriptions from this
formation are as follows:
LIMESTONE­light to medium gray with trace tan, dark gray
and black, cryptocrystalline to microcrystalline, varying
hardness from soft to firm, earthy to slightly dense texture,
grades from slightly to very argillaceous.
7 | P a g e
Lodgepole Formation
The "False Bakken" Marker (Mississippian Lodgepole Formation) is described as follows:
SHALE: black to brown black, soft to friable, earthy texture, slightly calcareous. This Marker is important for
making final adjustments to the landing TVD. Any drastic change here allows time for the directional drillers to
adjust their approach to landing the curve.
The Mississippian-Devonian Bakken Formation is comprised of two black carbonaceous and petroliferous
shales containing a silty, calcite and dolomite-cemented sandstone middle member with some inter-crystalline
porosity. This lithology is characterized by high gamma and elevated gas shows. A typical sample is described as
follows: SHALE - black, firm, sub blocky, earthy texture, common disseminated pyrite, calcareous,
carbonaceous, petroliferous, and no visible porosity.
Upper Bakken Shale
The Upper Bakken Shale has two distinctive peaks with the
lower peak ranging between 350 ­ 500 API. The samples showed
a blocky, very dark gray to black shale with no discernible flow or
depositional pattern.
Middle Bakken:
The Middle Bakken siltstones are consistent within the first 3-5'.
The gamma signature of the zone was typically a 50 ­ 150 API
gamma signature. Close inspection of the samples under a
microscope consistently showed a distinctive light colored, fine
grained silt stone.
.
The Sandstones unit of the Middle Bakken formation was found
to be 9' ­ 10' thick with a consistent gamma signature of approx.
60-80 API. No distinct gamma marker was found through this
unit consisting of an argillaceous medium gray limestone.

9 | P a g e
Interpreted Cross Section
The target zone was chosen based on density porosity logs from other wells within the manning Field.
Stratigraphic location of the target was based primarily on gamma ray values but gas shows, sample
observations, and drill rates were also utilized. The presence of distinct gamma ray indicators within the
Middle Bakken Formation help provide for dip calculations when present. The Limestone stringer which
is a clear low gamma marker seemed to always be present which allowed for accurate dip calculations.
(Interpreted dip calculation and measured depth are shown on pages 19)
10 | P a g e
11 | P a g e
Summary
1) The Oxy USA Inc. State Dvorak A 4-16-21H-142-96 consists of drilling a vertical, curve
and lateral section in the Middle Bakken formation.
2) Liners were run post TD.
3) State Dvorak A 4-16-21H-142-96 was spud on November 10th, 2014. Curve section was
started on November 20th, 2014 drilling the curve in 58 hours with one trip out. Lateral
drilling operations began on November 26th, 2014 and concluded on December 3rd, 2014 @
20,247' MD.
4) A diesel invert mud program was used through the drilling operation (~9.4 ­ 10.6 ppg) of the
vertical and curve section then brine water was used to drill the lateral.
5) Percentage in zone 100%
6) Gas throughout the well averaged 135 units with noted highest gas from 11,500-12,000
averaging 280 units.
7) Geo-steering was accomplished via sample evaluation and gamma markers. Dip estimations
were based on intersections with repeat markers by the well bore. Dip projections were
successfully utilized to maintain contact between the well bore and the target zone.
8) The State Dvorak A 4-16-21H-142-96 awaits completion operations to determine its
ultimate production potential.
Respectfully,
DHI Services, Inc.
January 3, 2014

Dear Elizabeth:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 25110, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval is
granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200' setback from
the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the 1280 acre spacing unit consisting
of Sections 16 & 21 T142N R96W. Tool error is not required pursuant to order.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock
disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during
clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are conducted. Due to drainage adjacent to
the well site, a dike is required surrounding the entire location. OXY USA INC must contact NDIC Field
Inspector Nicole Nelson at 701-290-1527 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling and
completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent pollution of
the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are prohibited. All pits shall be
inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized
in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The
proposed directional plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate
from the well head is: 10007'S and 320'W.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the approved
drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to commence before the 3rd
business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be waived by the Director.
Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to evaluate the extenuating
circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that would allow the Director to
conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested that
notification be given immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas
Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number,
drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00
p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours or on the weekend.
Elizabeth S. Bush-Ivie
October 15, 2014
Page 2
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall file a
certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be submitted as
one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the directional survey to be
filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the director's office in a timely manner.
Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or when
sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours, and tail
cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the plug or
initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov
Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks

I, William H. Dolinar, Professional Land Surveyor, ND. RLS #6550, hereby certify that (in accordance with a request from Cody Dennison with Oxy USA, Inc., 3239 Highway
22, Dickinson, North Dakota 58601) I and/or personnel under my direction made a survey on the 27th day of May 2014, for the Surface Hole Location and Elevation of platted
well, being located within the NW1/4NW1/4 of Section 16, T142N, R96W of the 5th P.M., Dunn County, State of North Dakota.
Notes: All Azimuths are based on the North line of Section 16, T142N, R96W of the 5th P.M., being an Azimuth of 269°57'48" using GPS observations, occupying a WHS
control point (5/8" rebar) and having the Location and Elevation derived from an OPUS Solution and GEOID 09. Azimuths shown have been rotated 1°43'26.05826" West
from SPC Grid bearings to Geodetic North, based on convergence angle provided by a conversion using Corpscon.
Project elevations are held on the control point located 268°29'02", 2362.33 Feet, from the Northeast Corner of Section 16, T142N, R96W of the 5th P.M. having a NAVD 88
elevation of 2414.02 feet.
Distances shown are Ground Distances using a combined scale factor of 1.000163806.
Location shown here on is not an "ASBUILT" location.
